# Code Block

<mark style="background: #D2B3FFA6;">VPN (GRE Tunnel):</mark>**
	- Connect the Private environment between sites through the internet environment by creating a Tunnel 1 interface tunnel including:
		- Tunnel Source
		- Tunnel Destination
		- IP của Tunnel --> Different from a normal interface in that it defines tunnel-source and tunnel-destination.
```bash
R1(config)#int tunnel 12
R1(config-if)#tunnel source 100.0.0.1 (or G0/1)
R1(config-if)#tunnel destination 200.0.0.1
R1(config-if)#tunnel mode gre ip (default) -> not to type configuration
R1(config-if)#ip address 192.168.12.1 255.255.255.0
			
R2(config)#int tunnel 12
R2(config-if)#tunnel source 200.0.0.1 (or g0/1)
R2(config-if)#tunnel destination 100.0.0.1
R2(config-if)#tunnel mode gre ip (default) -> not to type configuration
R2(config-if)#ip address 192.168.12.2 255.255.255.0
```


# Code Block 1

6. **<mark style="background: #D2B3FFA6;">VPN (GRE Tunnel):</mark>**
	- Connect the Private environment between sites through the internet environment by creating a Tunnel 1 interface tunnel including:
		- Tunnel Source
		- Tunnel Destination
		- IP của Tunnel --> Different from a normal interface in that it defines tunnel-source and tunnel-destination.
```bash
R1(config)#int tunnel 12
R1(config-if)#tunnel source 100.0.0.1 (or G0/1)
R1(config-if)#tunnel destination 200.0.0.1
R1(config-if)#tunnel mode gre ip (default) -> not to type configuration
R1(config-if)#ip address 192.168.12.1 255.255.255.0
			
R2(config)#int tunnel 12
R2(config-if)#tunnel source 200.0.0.1 (or g0/1)
R2(config-if)#tunnel destination 100.0.0.1
R2(config-if)#tunnel mode gre ip (default) -> not to type configuration
R2(config-if)#ip address 192.168.12.2 255.255.255.0
```


# Code Block 2

```5. **<mark style="background: #D2B3FFA6;">IPv6:</mark>** 
	- On the interface there will be 2 IPv6
	- 1 IPv6 is the Link-Local address automatically configured by Link-Local EUI-64EUI-64 is to split the MAC address, inserting between FF-FE and inverse bit number 7 of the MAC address --> Link-Local only has Only affects 1 Link, so when ping test, it will include Outbound-interface --> 1 Router can use 1 Link-Local address for the entire Interface.
	- The goal of the Link-Local address is to identify Routers with each other.
	- 1 IPv6 configured on the Interface (this IPv6 is used for routing) -> each Interface must have a different IPv6 address.
	
	- Bật IPv6: 
	  ```bash
	  Router(config)#ipv6 unicast routing
	  ```
	After typing this command, the Router's interfaces will generate a Link-Local EUI-64 address
	
	- Static Route:
		```bash
		Router(config)#ipv6 route <destination IPv6> /subnet "ipv6-next-hop"
		```
	
	- Dynamic Route:
		```bash
		R1(config)#ipv6 router ospf 1
		R1(config-router)#router-id 1.1.1.1
	
		R1(config)#int g0/0
		R1(config-if)#ipv6 ospf 1 area 0
	
		R2(config)#ipv6 router ospf 1
		R2(config-router)#router-id 2.2.2.2
	
		R2(config)#int g0/0
		R2(config-if)#ipv6 ospf 1 area 0
		```
5. **<mark style="background: #D2B3FFA6;">IPv6:</mark>** 
	- On the interface there will be 2 IPv6
	- 1 IPv6 is the Link-Local address automatically configured by Link-Local EUI-64EUI-64 is to split the MAC address, inserting between FF-FE and inverse bit number 7 of the MAC address --> Link-Local only has Only affects 1 Link, so when ping test, it will include Outbound-interface --> 1 Router can use 1 Link-Local address for the entire Interface.
	- The goal of the Link-Local address is to identify Routers with each other.
	- 1 IPv6 configured on the Interface (this IPv6 is used for routing) -> each Interface must have a different IPv6 address.
	
	- Bật IPv6: 
	  ```bash
	  Router(config)#ipv6 unicast routing
	  ```
	After typing this command, the Router's interfaces will generate a Link-Local EUI-64 address
	
	- Static Route:
		```bash
		Router(config)#ipv6 route <destination IPv6> /subnet "ipv6-next-hop"
		```
	
	- Dynamic Route:
		```bash
		R1(config)#ipv6 router ospf 1
		R1(config-router)#router-id 1.1.1.1
	
		R1(config)#int g0/0
		R1(config-if)#ipv6 ospf 1 area 0
	
		R2(config)#ipv6 router ospf 1
		R2(config-router)#router-id 2.2.2.2
	
		R2(config)#int g0/0
		R2(config-if)#ipv6 ospf 1 area 0
		```
```

# Excalidraw Data
## Text Elements
Spear ^j2yNgtsU

Egg ^vNfhYq81

- Hub n port    = 1 Broadcast Domain, 1 Collision Domain ^UFor3kbX

- Switch n port = 1 Broadcast Domain, n Collision Domain ^JPnUtns9

- Router n port = n Broadcast Domain, n Collision Domain ^IpTFvRyP

ARP resolves IP to MAC: throughout the entire process, the IP remains unchanged, only the MAC changes in each segment. ^ABulYDo3

Heart ^3JoBvnka

- The switch can only be plugged in and used, it cannot be configured and 
  only has 1 VLAN ^XDjaucb5

- Switches with VLAN configuration have 4096 - 2 = 4094 VLANs 
   (switchport access vlan vlan-id) ^L6UTqQXo

To conduct a VLAN, the two switches must access 1 VLAN at both ends (10 VLANs require 10 cables to conduct 10 VLANs). ^lieecPlm

Trunking was born to conduct 4094 VLANs on 1 wire (only costs 1 cable for 4094 VLANs). ^BolVEykx

Trunking: ISL (Cisco), Dot1q (Standard) ^VaV7QDbO

Vlan Synchronization on switch cisco ^f7RCYHzm

Router communication with Switch port trunk
assign vlan (layer 2) to router (layer 3) ^B3tCsdTs

Rulor ^RGajYUw2

ophidian ^sbQOvh5c

DHCP: Automatic IP allocation feature for a certain VLAN.

⇒ The first condition for DHCP to work is that Routing is completed.

⇒ For DHCP Relay Agent, go to the correct Gateway (where the DHCP 
    Server configures the Gateway parameters) to point to the DHCP Server. 
     (ip helpder-address “IP-DHCP-Server”) ^ERK9BduS

CDP - LLDP: Used to view device information ^f8Jv5H7E

Hook ^mXflR30o

Interface VLAN: Usually acts as a Gateway for the entire network.

2-layer model: Interface-vlan is configured at Switch-Core
3-layer model: Interface-vlan is usually configured at Switch-Distribution
 (can be configured on Switch-Core) ^B0AreJ2h

STP: Anti-loop in Layer 2 environment. ^JlPOdt5X

When the Switch is connected in a closed loop, a loop phenomenon
will occur. Solution: Temporarily block any port so that the connection is no longer a closed loop. ^7xVIcj9b

Hoe ^G8mIYxEe

Double Float ^v022wQlA

Cable: Etherchannel - port channel ^nbpSEmyy

Cisco: PAgP (desirable - auto) ^JJ73cAco

Standard: LaCP (active - passive) ^c0olMwmO

Switch: stackwise
Expansion: Switches do not necessarily have to be 
the same in terms of equipment, configuration, and port number
Backup: Switches must be the same in terms of device, 
configuration and port number. ^ejrLPTr7

Preventive Layer3 (Switch Layer3 / Router) - FHRP:
Cisco: HSRP Only supports 2 devices ( 1 Active - 1 Standby)
Standard: VRRP Supports up to about 16 devices (1 Active - the rest are Passive)
Solution: Generate 1 virtual GW representing 2 Routers (of which only Active Router is active). ^I1Yye2Kc

Trunking ^8f5ncXKT

VTP ^oFVsHYoo

Sub-Interface ^wDctdhQl

Increase redundancy (High Redundancy): ^iDlNMJXg

Duck ^jsVOafKS

Security Layer2 (originates right from the company) ^CzUDrnmf

MAC table attack: overflow the Switch's MAC table (When the Switch overflows the MAC, it will become a Hub) ^sKSe6cRt

Target: ^nXvyVkcX

- Convert Switch into Hub to capture information. ^KFITYVzz

- Causes the Switch to be Down (destructive attack). ^nGyt5YC1

- _Solution_: Limit the port speed, and use port Security to limit the number of MACs on a port. ^VCJNjMs1

Port Security: ^C2lMeXa1

1. MAC learning: default 1 MAC when port Security is enabled ^6wMF8JVz

- Static: Assign the MAC address directly to the port ^W1spLNOK

- Dynamic (default): Learn MAC, when reset, learn again -> lose MAC address when Switch resets or clears MAC table. ^MvFAZFV6

- Sticky: After learning the MAC, it will be saved forever (except when Admin deletes the MAC), combining learning MAC Dynamically and saving MAC Static. ^wE852Z1m

2. Impact: Protect, Restrict, Shutdown ^kFV0MS0y

- Protect: Does not send any information to the administrator, does not affect the port. ^P6fZvBo2

- Restrict: Does not affect the port, but does send a warning to the administrator. ^wFyuEvzC

- Shutdown: impact the port (err-disable: if you want to enable it again, shut down the port first and no shutdown again), and send a warning to the administrator. ^7jlpekRm

- Default of port Security: ^u2kRaWjF

```bash ^zCygvipk

Switch(config)#switchport port-security ^iiFJvFLK

``` ^2VEq2aOx

- Maximum number of MACs: 1 ^gzxRXoEu

- Learn MAC: Dynamic ^Fgagkcuw

- Action: Shutdown ^pzan941t

c. Change STP:

Attach a SW with the lowest MAC and Priority to the network port (will become the Root Switch), 
making all traffic in the network go through this Switch (to capture user information). 
→ Affects network access and slows down the network. 
Solutoin: Bật BPDU Guard trên port Access (Không nhận BPDU từ port ACcess) ^oNK6G7X7

b. VLAN Hopping: ^yGqI7xMg

Transform into Trunk port and use VLAN Native to detect user/Server information in other VLANs. Trunk ------ Access = N/A. Solution: configure all unused ports as Access ports and shutdown unused ports. ^6fFFGp9Z

d. DHCP snooping - ARP spoofing: ^iVXiWzl8

impersonate DHCP or a server to capture user information. ⇒ Solution: Enable dhcp snooping on Access port to prevent DHCP spoofing (prohibit setting static IP on dhcp snooping configuration ports - violation will result in Err-disable). ⇒ Trusted port trunk to receive DHCP from uplink, not receive DHCP from downlink. ^SdcigvKN

Ballons ^N0cb00Ir

Module3: Routing ^hcWc5eqy

1. Static Route: ^8AVNzjd2

- Routing is completely proactive at the discretion of the administrator. ^1Q8bL7pb

- --> Easy to configure for small and medium sized models ^zxKxygZK

- --> Easy to handle problems (due to complete initiative according to the administrator's wishes) ^JN40ZD68

- --> Difficult configuration for large network models. ^eQVrvQ6N

- --> Static Route is trashed (there are Routings that are no longer available but have not been deleted) but have not dared to delete them because I don't know if it will affect other parts or not. ^BvT5AXrj

- Fix: Always re-mark the static route statement. ^NiAmz9OI

Dynamic Route: OSPF ^N9OSIarD

- a. Router-id: ^J6xrJnyA

- IP Represents the Router when establishing neighbors between Routers participating in OSPF (selects the largest IP among the interfaces to be the router-id when not configuring the router-id). ^ABDELBcd

- b. DR-BDR: ^4Qig2RuK

- In the Broadcast MultiAccess segment, there will be DR and BDR elections ^CZtlhfhe

- DR: undertakes to receive all LSA from the DR-OTHER (224.0.0.5) and return routing information to the DR-OTHER (224.0.0.6) ^7filk9py

- BDR: only receive LSA from the DR-OTHER (224.0.0.5) and only respond when DR suffers Down. ^Jq78FOz0

- DR Only valid in 1 network segment, so configuring DR and BDR is to go to the interface to adjust Priority. ^51Yy1tMd

- Priority Default = 1 ^D86dUotL

- Priority = 0 (cannot participate in DR voting) ^hvIVnyWT

- Priority = 255 (greatest value) ^kUcX5qdg

- Router(config-if)#ip ospf priority 255 (definitely DR) ^p7qqZDxe

- Router(config-if)#ip ospf priority 0  (cannot participate in the election DR) ^blGH5Taf

- c. Point-to-Point: ^fz3rnSR2

- In a peer-to-peer environment, there is no DR/BDR election. In this environment, Routers send LSAs to each other and calculate their own routes and then send each other routing information. ^Z8OhyBEm

```bash ^Td7s5fTz

Router(config-if)#ip ospf network point-to-point ^PaRC4vR5

``` ^d7N1JoF3

- d. Cost của OSPF: ^FK22nRSE

```bash ^5dJNDZHH

reference BW (10^8) ^gTRcEGrL

Cost = _____________________ ^mE4yL64q

Interface BW ^o64N4dXM

``` ^f9NCJaDN

Refernce BW can be changed in Router mode ^hrL4YOmu

```bash ^fcbOPou2

Router(config)#router ospf 1 ^mIZRda51

Router(config-router)#ospf auto-cost reference-bandwidth 10000 (10GB) ^0o88fiPt

``` ^H5dGL1il

To change Cost to optimize routing along a certain route, go to the interface to configure. ^N6UoVHAZ

```bash ^u6AeZT7j

Router(config-if)#ip ospf cost 10 ^2Ip7mXbD

Access Control List (ACL): ^N7LO6g4C

- Used to filter traffic (Filter) or classify traffic (Classification) in the network according to the administrator's wishes. ^SEWwh6Jy

- a. Impact of ACL: Deny and Permit ^JHPSpfBf

- b. Form of ACL: ^oGkUAQ4b

- Standard: Can only define a single source IP (default destination IP is ANY) --> often used for subnet classification, VLAN classification (Classification) ^YFux0Uc3

- Extended: Definition includes: protocol (ip/icmp/tcp/udp), source IP, destination IP, port-ID/ping/time-exceeded/... --> traffic (Filter) ^lIRSWNxg

For example: write ACL to do the following: ^pxx4W9HA

- VLAN10: can access the web and ping (the rest cannot be accessed). ^wcUlbIPt

- VLAN20: have access to all services. ^kcerHS8B

- VLAN30: prohibit web access and traceroute. ^YVNWkjuG

172.16.VLAN-ID.0/24 ^fIHQGfre

```bash ^JzZGQ10K

Router(config)#ip access-list extended Local_LAN ^7JYFGo4N

Router(config-acl)#permit tcp   172.16.10.0 0.0.0.255 any eq www ^lk8pJ7Ae

Router(config-acl)#permit icmp 172.16.10.0  0.0.0.255 any ^66iZh7oE

Router(config-acl)#deny   ip   172.16.10.0  0.0.0.255 any ^XatEIbl2

Router(config-acl)#permit ip   172.16.20.0 0.0.0.255  any ^8zdLPktG

Router(config-acl)#deny   tcp  172.16.30.0 0.0.0.255  any eq www ^zEjYLVWQ

Router(config-acl)#deny   icmp 172.16.30.0 0.0.0.255  any traceroute ^AlyoqhfO

Router(config-acl)#permit ip   172.16.30.0 0.0.0.255  any ^OAA2WJR1

Router(config-acl)#deny ip any any (implicit deny - HIDDEN) ^KAmuPVdV

Network Address Translation (NAT): ^K94CwVRA

- convert IP/port-A to IP/port-B ^icqlF59q

- Source NAT: if >1 then define = ACL ^ZkzCSuEr

- Destination NAT: if >1 then define = POOL ^L50sV0Ad

- a. Static NAT: 1 -> 1 ^jtFwsLXQ

- Source:       n IP-A = 1 -> not defined ACL ^nkurStLg

- Destination:  n IP-B = 1 -> not defined Pool ^78hkKTsu

```bash ^GcrvFIWZ

Router(config)#ip nat inside source static 172.16.1.1 100.0.0.1 ^VusAzbsn

``` ^BoFiRDrl

- b. Dynamic NAT: n IP-A -> n IP-B ^vGRFD8w8

- Source:      n IP-A > 1 -> define ACL ^MOtbtkUM

- Destination: n IP-B > 1 -> define Pool ^jbgDHH3S

172.16.1.1 - 172.16.1.12 to IP 100.0.0.2 - 100.0.0.13 ^7zjMf3pX

```bash ^nKFOFfgT

Router(config)#ip access-list standard NAT-1.1-1.12 ^Rgx81yF5

Router(config-acl)#permit 172.16.1.0 0.0.0.15 ^uYnL1UlC

Router(config-acl)#ip nat pool MY_POOL 100.0.0.2 100.0.0.13 subnet-mask 255.255.255.240 ^KgwM7x1J

Router(config-acl)#ip nat pool MY_POOL 100.0.0.2 100.0.0.13 prefix-length 28 ^VO8jgGtu

Router(config)#ip nat inside source list NAT-1.1-1.12 MY_POOL ^lmWWNkUe

``` ^CPmlv3iu

- c. NAT overload: n IP-A -> 1 IP-B ^P7c9C4WI

- Source:       n IP-A > 1 -> define ACL ^1GJ3A18h

- Destination:  n IP-B = 1 -> not defined Pool ^4ueMbheF

- 172.16.1.0/24 NAT go out with interface g0/0 connecting to the network ^e7mClvJO

- 172.16.2.0/24 NAT go out with the remaining Public IP 100.0.0.14 ^F1fvwOOX

```bash ^8Guq10cB

Router(config)#ip access-list standard Internet_1.0 ^0oqLuopX

Router(config-acl)#permit 172.16.1.0 0.0.0.255 ^6bRiHP0p

Router(config)#ip nat inside source list Internet_1.0 interface g0/0 overload ^EPIuFU0s

Router(config)#ip access-list standard Internet_2.0 ^7SkdbLwe

Router(config-acl)#permit 172.16.1.0 0.0.0.255 ^EHbxciU5

Router(config)#ip nat inside source list Internet_2.0 100.0.0.14 ^CU2dkEq9

``` ^8YeqWoPq

- 1 IPv6 is the Link-Local address automatically configured by Link-Local EUI-64EUI-64 is to split the MAC address, inserting between FF-FE and inverse bit number 7 of the MAC address --> Link-Local only has Only affects 1 Link, so when ping test, it will include Outbound-interface --> 1 Router can use 1 Link-Local address for the entire Interface. ^jELH2SAk

- The goal of the Link-Local address is to identify Routers with each other. ^YnaC7nMU

- 1 IPv6 configured on the Interface (this IPv6 is used for routing) -> each Interface must have a different IPv6 address. ^7p4hXEed

6. VPN (GRE Tunnel): ^HO3Xr7ZX

- Connect the Private environment between sites through the internet environment by creating a Tunnel 1 interface tunnel including: ^1DhAktYa

- Tunnel Source ^K54eo30t

- Tunnel Destination ^FygpOF8O

- IP của Tunnel --> Different from a normal interface in that it defines tunnel-source and tunnel-destination. ^6ymb0Ltj

```bash ^kixJJ8pA

R1(config)#int tunnel 12 ^zgB5eApL

R1(config-if)#tunnel source 100.0.0.1 (or G0/1) ^MHTBEQQr

R1(config-if)#tunnel destination 200.0.0.1 ^ar4sNQTz

R1(config-if)#tunnel mode gre ip (default) -> not to type configuration ^TFd0uejr

R1(config-if)#ip address 192.168.12.1 255.255.255.0 ^XJ4IefKr

R2(config)#int tunnel 12 ^ZQ5flCZ4

R2(config-if)#tunnel source 200.0.0.1 (or g0/1) ^0Dh85n1c

R2(config-if)#tunnel destination 100.0.0.1 ^FE1IoQPZ

R2(config-if)#tunnel mode gre ip (default) -> not to type configuration ^KnHK2vmm

R2(config-if)#ip address 192.168.12.2 255.255.255.0 ^CDbB2RNq

- VTP has 3 modes: Server (Create VLAN, Sync VLAN), 
 Transparent (Create VLAN, Not Sync VLAN), 
Client (Not Create VLAN, Sync VLAN). ^jRP2cqWI

Step 1: ^dfsriBGU

-  Vote Root Switch ^8I6ySweA

-  Priority: lowest is best (n +/- 4096 apart, default priority Switch = 32768) ^vDOyJjvA

-  MAC: lowest is best. --> All ports of Root Switch are DP (Designated Port) ^iqEaYim8

Step 2: ^WgBUmBRk

-  Vote Root Port ^Qxocri8D

- Calculated by Cost: Cost is calculated from the Root Switch to the remaining ports, the lowest Cost is the best (Root Port - RP). ^p6BLd6Zb

Step 3: Block port (worst port) - Block all VLANs on this segment. ^yIs01cU3

- Cost: lowest is best ^mM5zL2O2

- Priority of Sender-ID: lowest is best ^TomybzU3

- MAC: lowest is best. ^NCpsq2KJ

Port status: ^SEdfDslw

1. From normal port to port Forwarding: 30s (Listening ->(15s) Learning ->(15s) Forwarding) ^TVTyA9Yr

2. From port Block to port Forwarding: 50s (Blocking ->(20s) Listening ->(15s) Learning ->(15s) Forwarding) ^3DN4kTer

- STP portfast: Used to make the Access port converge faster (only affects the Access port, does not affect the trunk port) ^QjoaZeLj

- Go to each port access interface to configure portfast ^TGxGKSC7

```bash ^6W3LS9hT

Switch(config-if)#spanning-tree portfast ^VSMf0T7b

``` ^oMsnHgaZ

- Configure portfast in config mode (apply on all access ports, except trunk port) ^9RvciNc0

```bash ^hT7y6wbr

Switch(config)#spanning-tree portfast default. ^beAQzYzw

``` ^BLMUt4FX

- Per-Vlan-STP (just Cisco support): PVSTP+ Each VLAN will have its own STP ^BMVUuyAt
